Callaway">Mickey Callaway</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">General Manager</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Sandy_Alderson" title="Sandy Alderson">Sandy Alderson</a> (<i>on leave</i>)<br /><b>Triumvirate</b> (<i>acting</i>)<br /><a href="/wiki/Omar_Minaya" title="Omar Minaya">Omar Minaya</a><br /><a href="/wiki/John_Ricco" title="John Ricco">John Ricco</a><br /><a href="/wiki/J._P._Ricciardi" title="J. P. Ricciardi">J. P. Ricciardi</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">President of Baseball Operations</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Saul_Katz" title="Saul Katz">Saul Katz</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>New York Mets</b> are an American professional <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> team based in the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> <a href="/wiki/Borough_(New_York_City)" class="mw-redirect" title="Borough (New York City)">borough</a> of <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a>. The Mets compete in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB) as a member club of the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> (NL) <a href="/wiki/National_League_East" title="National League East">East</a> division. The Mets are one of two Major League clubs based in New York City; the other is the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> of the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a>.\n</p><p>One of baseball\'s first <a href="/wiki/Expansion_team" title="Expansion team">expansion teams</a>, the Mets were founded in 1962 to replace New York\'s departed NL teams, the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Brooklyn_Dodgers" title="History of the Brooklyn Dodgers">Brooklyn Dodgers</a> and the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_New_York_Giants_(NL)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the New York Giants (NL)">New York Giants</a>. The Mets\' colors are composed of the <a href="/wiki/Dodger_blue" title="Dodger blue">Dodgers\' blue</a> and the Giants\' orange, which also form the outer two bands of the <a href="/wiki/Flags_of_New_York_City" title="Flags of New York City">New York City flag</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline1_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline1-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> During the 1962 and 1963 seasons, the Mets played their home games at the <a href="/wiki/Polo_Grounds" title="Polo Grounds">Polo Grounds</a>. From 1964 to 2008, the Mets\' home ballpark was <a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">Shea Stadium</a>. In 2009, they moved into their current ballpark, <a href="/wiki/Citi_Field" title="Citi Field">Citi Field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline1_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline1-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In their <a href="/wiki/1962_New_York_Mets_season" title="1962 New York Mets season">1962 inaugural season</a>, the Mets posted a record of 40\xe2\x80\x93120, the worst regular season record since MLB went to a 162-game schedule (two games were canceled). The team never finished better than second to last until the <a href="/wiki/1969_New_York_Mets_season" title="1969 New York Mets season">1969 "Miracle Mets"</a> beat the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1969_World_Series" title="1969 World Series">1969 World Series</a> in what is considered one of the biggest upsets in World Series history.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Since then, they have played in four additional World Series, including a dramatic run in <a href="/wiki/1973_World_Series" title="1973 World Series">1973</a> that ended in a seven-game loss to the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Oakland Athletics</a>, a second championship in <a href="/wiki/1986_World_Series" title="1986 World Series">1986</a> over the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Subway_Series" title="Subway Series">Subway Series</a> loss against their <a href="/wiki/Mets-Yankees_rivalry" class="mw-redirect" title="Mets-Yankees rivalry">cross-town rivals</a> the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> in <a href="/wiki/2000_World_Series" title="2000 World Series">2000</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and a five-game loss to the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a> in <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Series" title="2015 World Series">2015</a>.\n</p><p>The Mets qualified to play in the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_postseason" title="Major League Baseball postseason">Major League Baseball postseason</a> in <a href="/wiki/2006_New_York_Mets_season" title="2006 New York Mets season">2006</a>, when they came within one game of the World Series, losing to the eventual champion <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2006_National_League_Championship_Series" title="2006 National League Championship Series">NLCS</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The Mets missed the playoffs with losses on the last day of the regular season in 2007 and 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The Mets made the playoffs in <a href="/wiki/2015_New_York_Mets_season" title="2015 New York Mets season">2015</a> for the first time in nine years, and won their first NL pennant in 15 years. The team again returned to the playoffs in <a href="/wiki/2016_New_York_Mets_season" title="2016 New York Mets season">2016</a>, this time with a wild card berth. This was the team\'s second back-to-back playoff appearance, the first occurring during the 1999 and 2000 seasons.\n</p><p>For 1962\xe2\x80\x932018 the Mets overall win-loss record is 4362\xe2\x80\x934732 (0.480 win "percentage").<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Franchise_history"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Mascot"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Mascot</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Logo</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#Uniform_color_and_design"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span note</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Team_captains"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Team captains</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Baseball_Hall_of_Famers"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Baseball Hall of Famers</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Retired_numbers"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Retired numbers</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-11"><a href="#Numbers_out_of_circulation_but_not_retired"><span class="tocnumber">5.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Numbers out of circulation but not retired</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Rivalries"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Rivalries</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Subway_Series:_New_York_Yankees"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Subway Series: New York Yankees</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Atlanta_Braves"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Atlanta Braves</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Philadelphia_Phillies"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Philadelphia Phillies</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Staff"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Staff</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Current_roster"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Current roster</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#New_York_Mets_Foundation"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">New York Mets Foundation</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Owners_and_executives"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Owners and executives</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#New_York_Mets_broadcasters"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">New York Mets broadcasters</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Television"><span class="tocnumber">11.1</span> <span class="toctext">Television</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Radio"><span class="tocnumber">11.2</span> <span class="toctext">Radio</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Minor_league_affiliations"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Minor league affiliations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Franchise_history">Franchise history</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_New_York_Mets" title="History of the New York Mets">History of the New York Mets</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Shea.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/William_Shea.jpg/170px-William_Shea.jpg" width="170" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/William_Shea.jpg/255px-William_Shea.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/William_Shea.jpg/340px-William_Shea.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2064" data-file-height="2777" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Shea.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/William_Shea" title="William Shea">William Shea</a> was instrumental in returning <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League baseball</a> to <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> after five years of absence.</div></div></div>\n<p>After the 1957 season, the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Brooklyn_Dodgers" title="History of the Brooklyn Dodgers">Brooklyn Dodgers</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_New_York_Giants_(NL)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the New York Giants (NL)">New York Giants</a> <a href="/wiki/Relocation_of_professional_sports_teams" title="Relocation of professional sports teams">relocated</a> from New York to California to become the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a>, respectively, leaving the largest city in the United States with no National League franchise and only one major league team, the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> of the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> (AL). With the threat of a New York team joining a new <a href="/wiki/Continental_League" title="Continental League">third league</a>, the National League <a href="/wiki/1962_Major_League_Baseball_expansion" title="1962 Major League Baseball expansion">expanded</a> by adding the New York Mets following a proposal from <a href="/wiki/William_Shea" title="William Shea">William Shea</a>. In a symbolic reference to New York\'s earlier National League teams, the new team took as its primary colors the blue of the Dodgers and the orange of the Giants, colors also featured on the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_New_York_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Flag of New York City">Flag of New York City</a>. The nickname "Mets" was adopted: it was a natural shorthand to the club\'s corporate name, "The New York Metropolitan Baseball Club, Inc.",<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> hearkened back to the "<a href="/wiki/New_York_Metropolitans" title="New York Metropolitans">Metropolitans</a>" (a former New York team in the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_(19th_century)" title="American Association (19th century)">American Association</a> from 1880 to 1887),<sup id="cite_ref-timeline1_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline1-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> and its brevity was advantageous for newspaper headlines.<sup id="cite_ref-Nickname_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nickname-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shea_stadium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Shea_stadium.jpg/170px-Shea_stadium.jpg" width="170" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Shea_stadium.jpg/255px-Shea_stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Shea_stadium.jpg/340px-Shea_stadium.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1980" data-file-height="2891" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shea_stadium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">Shea Stadium</a> was the Mets\' home field from 1964 to 2008.</div></div></div>\n<p>For the first two years of its existence, the team played its home games at the historic <a href="/wiki/Polo_Grounds" title="Polo Grounds">Polo Grounds</a> in <a href="/wiki/Upper_Manhattan" title="Upper Manhattan">Upper Manhattan</a>. In 1964, they moved into newly constructed <a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">Shea Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Flushing,_Queens" title="Flushing, Queens">Flushing, Queens</a>, where the Mets played until the 2008 season. In 2009, the club moved into <a href="/wiki/Citi_Field" title="Citi Field">Citi Field</a>, adjacent to the former Shea Stadium site.\n</p><p>During their history, the Mets have won two <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> titles (<a href="/wiki/1969_World_Series" title="1969 World Series">1969</a> and <a href="/wiki/1986_World_Series" title="1986 World Series">1986</a>), five National League <a href="/wiki/National_League_Championship_Series" title="National League Championship Series">pennants</a> (<a href="/wiki/1969_NLCS" class="mw-redirect" title="1969 NLCS">1969</a>, <a href="/wiki/1973_NLCS" class="mw-redirect" title="1973 NLCS">1973</a>, <a href="/wiki/1986_NLCS" class="mw-redirect" title="1986 NLCS">1986</a>, <a href="/wiki/2000_NLCS" class="mw-redirect" title="2000 NLCS">2000</a>, <a href="/wiki/2015_NLCS" class="mw-redirect" title="2015 NLCS">2015</a>) and six <a href="/wiki/National_League_East" title="National League East">National League East</a> titles (1969, 1973, 1986, 1988, 2006, 2015). The Mets also qualified for the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_postseason" title="Major League Baseball postseason">postseason</a> as the National League <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_wild_card" title="Major League Baseball wild card">wild card</a> team in 1999, 2000, and 2016. The Mets have appeared in five World Series, more than any other <a href="/wiki/Expansion_team" title="Expansion team">expansion team</a> in MLB history. Their two championships are the most titles among expansion teams, equal to the tallies of the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miami_Marlins" title="Miami Marlins">Miami Marlins</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Mets held the New York baseball single-season attendance record for 29 years. They broke the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">Yankees</a>\' 1948 record by drawing nearly 2.7 million spectators in 1970. The Mets broke their own record five times before the record was regained by the Yankees in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-BRNYMattend_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BRNYMattend-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BRNYYattend_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BRNYYattend-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tom_Seaver_at_Shea_Stadium_1974_CROP.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Tom_Seaver_at_Shea_Stadium_1974_CROP.jpg/170px-Tom_Seaver_at_Shea_Stadium_1974_CROP.jpg" width="170" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Tom_Seaver_at_Shea_Stadium_1974_CROP.jpg/255px-Tom_Seaver_at_Shea_Stadium_1974_CROP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b5/Tom_Seaver_at_Shea_Stadium_1974_CROP.jpg 2x" data-file-width="320" data-file-height="418" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tom_Seaver_at_Shea_Stadium_1974_CROP.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tom_Seaver" title="Tom Seaver">Tom Seaver</a> led the Mets to victory in the <a href="/wiki/1969_World_Series" title="1969 World Series">1969 World Series</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/1962_New_York_Mets_season" title="1962 New York Mets season">1962 Mets</a> posted a 40\xe2\x80\x93120 record, a record for the most losses in a season since 1899. In 1966, the Mets famously bypassed future Hall of Famer <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Jackson" title="Reggie Jackson">Reggie Jackson</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1966_Major_League_Baseball_draft" title="1966 Major League Baseball draft">amateur draft</a>, instead selecting <a href="/wiki/Steve_Chilcott" title="Steve Chilcott">Steve Chilcott</a>, who never played in the majors. But the following year, they acquired future Hall of Famer <a href="/wiki/Tom_Seaver" title="Tom Seaver">Tom Seaver</a> in a lottery. Seaver helped the <a href="/wiki/1969_New_York_Mets_season" title="1969 New York Mets season">1969 "Miracle Mets"</a> win the new <a href="/wiki/National_League_East" title="National League East">National League East</a> division title, then defeat the <a href="/wiki/1969_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="1969 Atlanta Braves season">Atlanta Braves</a> to win the National League pennant and the heavily favored <a href="/wiki/1969_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1969 Baltimore Orioles season">Baltimore Orioles</a> to win the <a href="/wiki/1969_World_Series" title="1969 World Series">1969 World Series</a>.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/1973_New_York_Mets_season" title="1973 New York Mets season">1973</a>, the Mets rallied from 5th place to win the division, despite a record of only 82\xe2\x80\x9379. They shocked the heavily favored <a href="/wiki/1973_Cincinnati_Reds_season" title="1973 Cincinnati Reds season">Cincinnati Reds</a> "<a href="/wiki/The_Big_Red_Machine" class="mw-redirect" title="The Big Red Machine">Big Red Machine</a>" in the <a href="/wiki/1973_National_League_Championship_Series" title="1973 National League Championship Series">NLCS</a> and pushed the defending World Series champion <a href="/wiki/1973_Oakland_Athletics_season" title="1973 Oakland Athletics season">Oakland Athletics</a> to a seventh game, but lost the series. Notably, 1973 was the only NL East title between 1970 and 1980 that wasn\'t won by either the <a href="/wiki/Phillies%E2%80%93Pirates_rivalry" title="Phillies\xe2\x80\x93Pirates rivalry">Philadelphia Phillies or the Pittsburgh Pirates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Star pitcher Tom Seaver was traded in <a href="/wiki/1977_New_York_Mets_season" title="1977 New York Mets season">1977</a>, on a day remembered as "the Midnight Massacre",<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and the Mets fell into last place for several years. The franchise turned around in the mid-1980s. During this time the Mets also drafted slugger <a href="/wiki/Darryl_Strawberry" title="Darryl Strawberry">Darryl Strawberry</a> (#1 in 1980) and 1985 <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young_Award" title="Cy Young Award">Cy Young Award</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Dwight_Gooden" title="Dwight Gooden">Dwight Gooden</a> (#5 in 1982). In addition, former National League MVP and perennial <a href="/wiki/Gold_Glove" class="mw-redirect" title="Gold Glove">Gold Glove</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Keith_Hernandez" title="Keith Hernandez">Keith Hernandez</a> was obtained by the Mets in 1983.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/1985_New_York_Mets_season" title="1985 New York Mets season">1985</a>, they acquired Hall of Fame catcher <a href="/wiki/Gary_Carter" title="Gary Carter">Gary Carter</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">Montreal Expos</a> and won 98 games, but narrowly missed the playoffs. In <a href="/wiki/1986_New_York_Mets_season" title="1986 New York Mets season">1986</a>, they easily won the division with a record of 108\xe2\x80\x9354, one of the best in National League history. They won a dramatic <a href="/wiki/1986_National_League_Championship_Series" title="1986 National League Championship Series">NLCS</a> in six games over the <a href="/wiki/1986_Houston_Astros_season" title="1986 Houston Astros season">Houston Astros</a>. The sixth game of the series went sixteen innings, the longest playoff game in history until 2005. They came within one strike of losing the <a href="/wiki/1986_World_Series" title="1986 World Series">World Series</a> against the <a href="/wiki/1986_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="1986 Boston Red Sox season">Boston Red Sox</a> before a series of hits and defensive miscues ultimately led to an error by Boston\'s <a href="/wiki/Bill_Buckner" title="Bill Buckner">Bill Buckner</a> which gave the Mets a game 6 victory. They then won Game 7 to win their second World Series title.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mike_Piazza_spring_of_2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Mike_Piazza_spring_of_2004.jpg/170px-Mike_Piazza_spring_of_2004.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Mike_Piazza_spring_of_2004.jpg/255px-Mike_Piazza_spring_of_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/05/Mike_Piazza_spring_of_2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="267" data-file-height="400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mike_Piazza_spring_of_2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mike_Piazza" title="Mike Piazza">Mike Piazza</a> playing for the Mets in 2004.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Mets continued playing well after 1986 and won the division in <a href="/wiki/1988_New_York_Mets_season" title="1988 New York Mets season">1988</a>, but were <a href="/wiki/1988_NLCS" class="mw-redirect" title="1988 NLCS">eliminated from the playoffs</a> that year and declined into the 1990s. They were out of contention until the <a href="/wiki/1997_New_York_Mets_season" title="1997 New York Mets season">1997 season</a> when they were in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_wild_card" title="Major League Baseball wild card">wild card</a> contention until the final week of the season. In <a href="/wiki/1998_New_York_Mets_season" title="1998 New York Mets season">1998</a>, the Mets acquired catcher <a href="/wiki/Mike_Piazza" title="Mike Piazza">Mike Piazza</a> in a blockbuster trade and missed the postseason by only one game. In <a href="/wiki/1999_New_York_Mets_season" title="1999 New York Mets season">1999</a>, they made the playoffs after <a href="/wiki/1999_National_League_Wild_Card_tie-breaker_game" title="1999 National League Wild Card tie-breaker game">a one-game playoff</a> but lost the <a href="/wiki/1999_National_League_Championship_Series" title="1999 National League Championship Series">1999 National League Championship Series</a> to the <a href="/wiki/1999_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="1999 Atlanta Braves season">Atlanta Braves</a>. In <a href="/wiki/2000_New_York_Mets_season" title="2000 New York Mets season">2000</a>, they easily clinched a wild card spot in the playoffs, and earned a trip to the <a href="/wiki/2000_World_Series" title="2000 World Series">2000 World Series</a> against their crosstown rivals, the New York Yankees for a "<a href="/wiki/Subway_Series" title="Subway Series">Subway Series</a>". The Mets were defeated by the Yankees in five games.\n</p><p>The Mets had a near playoff miss in 2001 and struggled from 2002 to 2004. In the aftermath of the 2004 season, the Mets hired a new general manager, <a href="/wiki/Omar_Minaya" title="Omar Minaya">Omar Minaya</a>, who immediately turned the franchise around by signing pitcher <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Pedro Mart\xc3\xadnez">Pedro Mart\xc3\xadnez</a> and hiring a new manager, <a href="/wiki/Willie_Randolph" title="Willie Randolph">Willie Randolph</a>. The Mets finished 2005 four games over .500, and the franchise\'s resurgence was complete by 2006 as they won 97 games and the NL East title behind new acquisitions <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Beltr%C3%A1n" title="Carlos Beltr\xc3\xa1n">Carlos Beltr\xc3\xa1n</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Delgado" title="Carlos Delgado">Carlos Delgado</a>, as well as young superstars <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Reyes_(shortstop)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Reyes (shortstop)">Jos\xc3\xa9 Reyes</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Wright" title="David Wright">David Wright</a>. The Mets advanced to game seven of the <a href="/wiki/2006_NLCS" class="mw-redirect" title="2006 NLCS">2006 NLCS</a> but lost after <a href="/wiki/Yadier_Molina" title="Yadier Molina">Yadier Molina</a>\'s game-winning two-run home run in the top of the ninth inning. The Mets loaded the bases with two outs in the bottom of the inning, but <a href="/wiki/Adam_Wainwright" title="Adam Wainwright">Adam Wainwright</a> struck out Beltran looking with a devastating <a href="/wiki/Curveball" title="Curveball">curveball</a>.\n</p><p>In 2007, the Mets entered the final 17 games in the season with a seven-game lead in the division. But the team went on an ill-timed losing streak, losing 11 of the next 15 games and needing to win their final two games to make the playoffs. The Mets won their penultimate game, but on the final day of the season, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Glavine" title="Tom Glavine">Tom Glavine</a> gave up seven runs in the first inning en route to an 8\xe2\x80\x931 loss that eliminated the team from contention. The Philadelphia Phillies won the division by one game after a win on the season\'s last day.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Wright_warmup_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/David_Wright_warmup_2.jpg/170px-David_Wright_warmup_2.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/David_Wright_warmup_2.jpg/255px-David_Wright_warmup_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/David_Wright_warmup_2.jpg/340px-David_Wright_warmup_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="682" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Wright_warmup_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/David_Wright" title="David Wright">David Wright</a> was the most recent Mets captain before retiring in 2018.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Mets held a more modest 3.5-game lead after 145 games of the <a href="/wiki/2008_New_York_Mets_season" title="2008 New York Mets season">2008 season</a>, their final season at <a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">Shea Stadium</a>. While their 7\xe2\x80\x9310 mark down the stretch was better than the previous season\'s 5\xe2\x80\x9312, it still allowed the Phillies to pass them once again for the division crown, which they lost by three games. The Mets opened <a href="/wiki/Citi_Field" title="Citi Field">Citi Field</a> in 2009, but were not a factor due to a rash of injuries to numerous key players including Reyes, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Beltr%C3%A1n" title="Carlos Beltr\xc3\xa1n">Carlos Beltr\xc3\xa1n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Delgado" title="Carlos Delgado">Carlos Delgado</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%93liver_P%C3%A9rez" title="\xc3\x93liver P\xc3\xa9rez">\xc3\x93liver P\xc3\xa9rez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liv%C3%A1n_Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="Liv\xc3\xa1n Hern\xc3\xa1ndez">Liv\xc3\xa1n Hern\xc3\xa1ndez</a>. The effect of the injuries plummeted the Mets to a 70\xe2\x80\x9392 record. The Mets improved to a 79\xe2\x80\x9383 in 2010, but still finished in fourth place, missing the playoffs for the fourth straight year.\n</p><p>After the 2010 season, the Mets fired Minaya and manager <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Manuel" title="Jerry Manuel">Jerry Manuel</a>. Former <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Oakland Athletics</a> G.M. and MLB executive <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Alderson" title="Sandy Alderson">Sandy Alderson</a> was hired to run the team, who hired <a href="/wiki/Terry_Collins" title="Terry Collins">Terry Collins</a> as manager.\n</p><p>In 2012, Mets owners <a href="/wiki/Fred_Wilpon" title="Fred Wilpon">Fred Wilpon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saul_Katz" title="Saul Katz">Saul Katz</a> settled a lawsuit brought against them on behalf of the victims of <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Madoff" title="Bernard Madoff">Bernard Madoff</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Ponzi_scheme" title="Ponzi scheme">Ponzi scheme</a> for $162 million. As a result of this agreement the liquidator, <a href="/wiki/Irving_Picard" title="Irving Picard">Irving Picard</a>, agreed to drop the charges that Wilpon and Katz blindly went along with the scheme for their personal benefit. Picard had originally sought to recover $1 billion from the Wilpon family and Katz, but settled for $162 million along with the admission that neither the Wilpons nor Katz had any knowledge of the Ponzi scheme. In 2011\xe2\x80\x932012, Mets ownership sold twelve minority 4% shares (48%) of the franchise at $20 million apiece to provide a cash infusion of $240 million for the team.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite yet another losing season, the Mets made history in 2011 when closer <a href="/wiki/Jason_Isringhausen" title="Jason Isringhausen">Jason Isringhausen</a> converted his <a href="/wiki/300_save_club" title="300 save club">300th save</a> with the team, the third player in franchise history to reach the milestone while with the organization (after <a href="/wiki/John_Franco" title="John Franco">John Franco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Billy_Wagner" title="Billy Wagner">Billy Wagner</a>). Also, Reyes became the first Met in franchise history to win a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_batting_champions" title="List of Major League Baseball batting champions">National League batting title</a>, posting a .337 <a href="/wiki/Batting_average" title="Batting average">batting average</a>. In 2012, as the Mets tried to bounce back from three consecutive losing seasons, they lost star shortstop Reyes to free agency, when he signed with the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Marlins" title="Miami Marlins">Miami Marlins</a>. The team started out strong, getting a career-year performance from the league\'s only knuckleballer, <a href="/wiki/R.A._Dickey" title="R.A. Dickey">R.A. Dickey</a>, and strong production from Wright. But they faltered midseason and ended with a 74\xe2\x80\x9388 record, again finishing fourth in the division.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Johan_Santana_on_May_5,_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Johan_Santana_on_May_5%2C_2012.jpg/170px-Johan_Santana_on_May_5%2C_2012.jpg" width="170" height="276" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Johan_Santana_on_May_5%2C_2012.jpg/255px-Johan_Santana_on_May_5%2C_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Johan_Santana_on_May_5%2C_2012.jpg/340px-Johan_Santana_on_May_5%2C_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1850" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Johan_Santana_on_May_5,_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Johan_Santana" title="Johan Santana">Johan Santana</a> threw the only <a href="/wiki/No-hitter" title="No-hitter">no-hitter</a> in Mets history in 2012.</div></div></div>\n<p>Prior to the <a href="/wiki/2012_New_York_Mets_season" title="2012 New York Mets season">2012 season</a> the Mets had yet to throw a <a href="/wiki/No-hitter" title="No-hitter">no-hitter</a>, and the franchise\'s hurlers had gone 8,019<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> games without pitching one \xe2\x80\x93 longer than any other major-league franchise. They were one of only two major-league teams to never have a pitcher throw a no-hitter (the other being the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a>). However, on June 1, 2012 <a href="/wiki/Johan_Santana" title="Johan Santana">Johan Santana</a> pitched a no-hitter against the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a>. Averting the spotlight from <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Beltr%C3%A1n" title="Carlos Beltr\xc3\xa1n">Carlos Beltr\xc3\xa1n</a>\'s return to Citi Field, Santana turned a routine game into a memorable moment in Mets history. Santana risked being removed from the game after he went over his limit of 110 pitches, placed by the team because of his shoulder surgery. Still Santana stayed in the game and threw 134 total pitches that evening in an 8\xe2\x80\x930 Mets victory, helped by a few great defensive plays as well as a controversial foul-ball call (coincidentally on Beltran), to pull off the first no-hitter in Mets history.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> That was the high point of 2012 along with pitcher <a href="/wiki/R.A._Dickey" title="R.A. Dickey">R.A. Dickey</a> winning the National League <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young_Award" title="Cy Young Award">Cy Young Award</a>. This would be Dickey\'s final season as a Mets though as he along with <a href="/wiki/Josh_Thole" title="Josh Thole">Josh Thole</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Nickeas" title="Mike Nickeas">Mike Nickeas</a> were traded to the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Blue_Jays" title="Toronto Blue Jays">Toronto Blue Jays</a> for prospects <a href="/wiki/Travis_d%27Arnaud" title="Travis d&#39;Arnaud">Travis d\'Arnaud</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noah_Syndergaard" title="Noah Syndergaard">Noah Syndergaard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wuilmer_Becerra" class="mw-redirect" title="Wuilmer Becerra">Wuilmer Becerra</a>, and veteran catcher <a href="/wiki/John_Buck_(baseball)" title="John Buck (baseball)">John Buck</a>. The <a href="/wiki/2013_New_York_Mets_season" title="2013 New York Mets season">2013 season</a> brought another 74\xe2\x80\x9388 finish but they were able to finish in 3rd place. The highlight of the season was sweeping the season series between their cross town rivals Yankees, a first since interleague play started in 1997.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jacob_deGrom.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Jacob_deGrom.jpg/170px-Jacob_deGrom.jpg" width="170" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Jacob_deGrom.jpg/255px-Jacob_deGrom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Jacob_deGrom.jpg/340px-Jacob_deGrom.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1401" data-file-height="2114" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jacob_deGrom.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jacob_deGrom" title="Jacob deGrom">Jacob deGrom</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Rookie_of_the_Year_Award" title="Major League Baseball Rookie of the Year Award">2014 National League Rookie of the Year</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Prior to the start of the <a href="/wiki/2014_New_York_Mets_season" title="2014 New York Mets season">2014 season</a> the Mets made a big splash in the free agent market by signing former <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> outfielder <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Granderson" title="Curtis Granderson">Curtis Granderson</a> to a 4-year $60 million contract. They also signed former <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Oakland Athletics</a> starting pitcher <a href="/wiki/Bartolo_Col%C3%B3n" title="Bartolo Col\xc3\xb3n">Bartolo Col\xc3\xb3n</a> to a 2-year deal to help offset losing ace pitcher <a href="/wiki/Matt_Harvey" title="Matt Harvey">Matt Harvey</a> for the year after he required <a href="/wiki/Tommy_John_surgery" class="mw-redirect" title="Tommy John surgery">Tommy John surgery</a>. They would improve to 79\xe2\x80\x9383 and finish the season tied for 2nd place with Atlanta but it was their 6th consecutive season where they finished under .500. Pitcher <a href="/wiki/Jacob_deGrom" title="Jacob deGrom">Jacob deGrom</a> would win the <a href="/wiki/National_League_Rookie_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="National League Rookie of the Year">National League Rookie of the Year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On April 23, 2015 the Mets tied a franchise season record of eleven straight wins. For the first time in its history the Mets won ten straight homestand games, becoming the 7th team since 1900 to win at least 10 straight homestand games.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> On September 26, 2015, the Mets clinched the NL East division title, and thus their first postseason berth since 2006, by defeating the Cincinnati Reds 10\xe2\x80\x932. They defeated the Los Angeles Dodgers in the <a href="/wiki/2015_NLDS" class="mw-redirect" title="2015 NLDS">NLDS</a>, three games to two, and swept the Chicago Cubs in the <a href="/wiki/2015_NLCS" class="mw-redirect" title="2015 NLCS">NLCS</a> for their first pennant in 15 years. In the <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Series" title="2015 World Series">2015 World Series</a>, they were defeated by the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a> in five games. After the season ended, pitcher <a href="/wiki/Matt_Harvey" title="Matt Harvey">Matt Harvey</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Comeback_Player_of_the_Year_Award" title="Major League Baseball Comeback Player of the Year Award">NL Comeback Player of the Year</a> award. Outfielder <a href="/wiki/Yoenis_C%C3%A9spedes" title="Yoenis C\xc3\xa9spedes">Yoenis C\xc3\xa9spedes</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Rawlings_Gold_Glove_Award" title="Rawlings Gold Glove Award">NL Gold Glove</a> award as a left fielder.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Theme_song">Theme song</span></h2>\n<p>"<a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Mets" title="Meet the Mets">Meet the Mets</a>" is the Mets\' signature song, written in 1961, one year before the first season, by Bill Katz and <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Roberts" title="Ruth Roberts">Ruth Roberts</a>. It is played on the radio, during television broadcasts and at Mets\' home games.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot">Mascot</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For more information, see <a href="/wiki/Mr._Met" title="Mr. Met">Mr. Met</a>.</div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Mr._Met" title="Mr. Met">Mr. Met</a> is the official mascot of the New York Mets. He was introduced on the cover of game programs in 1963, when the Mets were still playing at the <a href="/wiki/Polo_Grounds" title="Polo Grounds">Polo Grounds</a> in northern Manhattan.<sup id="cite_ref-Mr._Met_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mr._Met-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> When the Mets moved to <a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">Shea Stadium</a> in 1964, fans were introduced to a live costumed version.<sup id="cite_ref-Mr._Met_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mr._Met-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Mr. Met is believed to have been the first mascot in Major League Baseball to exist in human (as opposed to artistically rendered) form.<sup id="cite_ref-Mr._Met_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mr._Met-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mrs._Met" title="Mrs. Met">Mrs. Met</a> (formerly Lady Met) is the female counterpart to Mr. Met, and the couple sometimes appears with 2\xe2\x80\x933 smaller "children".<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Uniform_and_logo_symbolism">Uniform and logo symbolism</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:145px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jerry_Koosman_2008-09-28.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Jerry_Koosman_2008-09-28.jpg/143px-Jerry_Koosman_2008-09-28.jpg" width="143" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Jerry_Koosman_2008-09-28.jpg/215px-Jerry_Koosman_2008-09-28.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Jerry_Koosman_2008-09-28.jpg/286px-Jerry_Koosman_2008-09-28.jpg 2x" data-file-width="633" data-file-height="1140" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jerry_Koosman_2008-09-28.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jerry_Koosman" title="Jerry Koosman">Jerry Koosman</a> wearing his late-1960s\' era Mets jersey, which served as an inspiration for the 2012\xe2\x80\x9313 Mets pinstriped uniform.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For more information, see <a href="/wiki/Logos_and_uniforms_of_the_New_York_Mets" title="Logos and uniforms of the New York Mets">Logos and uniforms of the New York Mets</a>.</div>\n<p>The Mets\' colors are blue and orange, originally chosen to honor the city\'s history of <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> baseball; blue for the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Dodgers" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Dodgers">Brooklyn Dodgers</a>, and orange for the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants_(NL)" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Giants (NL)">New York Giants</a>. Blue and orange are also the colors of New York City, as seen on its <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_New_York_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Flag of New York City">flag</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline1_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline1-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1998, black was officially added to the color scheme, although beginning with 2012 the black elements in the uniform began to be phased out, and were eliminated in 2013.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Logo">Logo</span></h3>\n<p>The cap logo is identical to the logo used by the New York Giants in their final years, and is on a blue cap reminiscent of the caps worn by the Brooklyn Dodgers. In the primary logo, designed by sports cartoonist Ray Gatto, each part of the skyline has special meaning\xe2\x80\x94at the left is a church spire, symbolic of Brooklyn, the borough of churches; the second building from the left is the Williamsburgh Savings Bank, the tallest building in Brooklyn; next is the Woolworth Building; after a general skyline view of midtown comes the Empire State Building; at the far right is the United Nations Building. The bridge in the center symbolizes that the Mets, by bringing National League baseball back to New York, represent all five boroughs.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline1_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline1-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>With the introduction of black as an official color, an alternate team logo was created in 1999. It is identical to the original logo, but the skyline is black instead of blue and the "Mets" script is blue trimmed in orange and white instead of orange trimmed in white (the alternate black jerseys displayed the primary blue and orange logo on the left sleeves in 1998; in 1999 this was changed to the alternate black and blue logo). The logo fell into disuse after the Mets dropped the alternate black jerseys and caps in 2012.\n</p><p>Also in 1999, the logo received a slight alteration. The "NY" to the left of the team script was removed. No other notable changes were made.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uniform_color_and_design">Uniform color and design</span></h3>\n<p>Currently, the Mets wear an assortment of uniforms.\n</p><p>The home uniforms are white with blue pinstripes, and feature the "Mets" script and block lettering and numbers in blue with orange outline. The uniforms are paired with a standard blue cap featuring the "NY" script in orange, plus blue undersleeves, belts and socks. The white pinstriped uniforms replaced both the cream pinstriped uniform and the alternate white uniform starting with the 2015 season.\n</p><p>The gray road jerseys feature a radially-arched "NEW YORK" script in Tiffany style, player numerals and names in blue outlined in orange, and blue placket and sleeve piping. Like the home uniforms, the road grays are worn with blue caps, undersleeves, belts and socks.\n</p><p>On November 14, 2012, the Mets introduced two new blue alternate jerseys. The home alternate features the "Mets" script, player numerals and names in orange outlined in white, while the road alternate feature the "NEW YORK" script, player numerals and names in gray outlined in orange.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On December 10, 2012, the Mets unveiled an alternate blue fielding cap, featuring an orange brim and a white trim around the orange "NY" insignia.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Currently it is only worn in games featuring the home blue alternates. For 2015, another alternate blue cap, this time featuring the "NY" in gray outlined in orange, was introduced, and is paired with the road blue alternates. In 2017, the alternate home blue cap was modified to feature a blue brim.\n</p><p>For the 2014 season, a <a href="/wiki/Mr._Met" title="Mr. Met">Mr. Met</a> sleeve patch was added to the blue alternate jerseys,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> a feature that was later removed in favor of the primary logo in 2017.\n</p><p>The Mets\' standard blue batting helmet with the "NY" in orange is currently used regardless of the cap and jersey design they wear. This was in contrast to previous seasons where they play with alternate batting helmets to match their caps and jerseys.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Players_of_note">Players of note</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_captains">Team captains</span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Keith_Hernandez" title="Keith Hernandez">Keith Hernandez</a> 1987\xe2\x80\x931989<sup id="cite_ref-Fourth_Captain_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fourth_Captain-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gary_Carter" title="Gary Carter">Gary Carter</a> 1988\xe2\x80\x931989<sup id="cite_ref-Fourth_Captain_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fourth_Captain-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/John_Franco" title="John Franco">John Franco</a> 2001\xe2\x80\x932004<sup id="cite_ref-Fourth_Captain_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fourth_Captain-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/David_Wright" title="David Wright">David Wright</a> 2013\xe2\x80\x932018<sup id="cite_ref-Fourth_Captain_30-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fourth_Captain-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Baseball_Hall_of_Famers">Baseball Hall of Famers</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Franco_2008-09-28.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/John_Franco_2008-09-28.jpg/220px-John_Franco_2008-09-28.jpg" width="220" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/John_Franco_2008-09-28.jpg/330px-John_Franco_2008-09-28.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/John_Franco_2008-09-28.jpg/440px-John_Franco_2008-09-28.jpg 2x" data-file-width="749" data-file-height="1021" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Franco_2008-09-28.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/John_Franco" title="John Franco">John Franco</a> during the final game at <a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">Shea Stadium</a>.</div></div></div>\n<table class="toccolours" style="font-size: 95%; margin: 1em auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="1" Mays">Willie Mays</a>\n</p>\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Eddie_Murray" title="Eddie Murray">Eddie Murray</a><br /><b><a href="/wiki/Mike_Piazza" width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Duke_Snider" title="Duke Snider">Duke Snider</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Warren_Spahn" title="Warren Spahn">Warren Spahn</a><br /><a style="font-size:87%;">Honored<br />March 31, 2014</span>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Citi_Field_retired_numbers_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Citi_Field_retired_numbers_2018.jpg/275px-Citi_Field_retired_numbers_2018.jpg" width="275" height="88" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Citi_Field_retired_numbers_2018.jpg/413px-Citi_Field_retired_numbers_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Citi_Field_retired_numbers_2018.jpg/550px-Citi_Field_retired_numbers_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8032" data-file-height="2571" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Citi_Field_retired_numbers_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Mets\' retired numbers at Citi Field, 2018</div></div></div>\n<p>Major League Baseball retired <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a>\'s number 42 on April 15, 1997, when the Mets played the <a href="/wiki/1997_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1997 Los Angeles Dodgers season">Dodgers</a> at <a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">Shea Stadium</a>. <a href="/wiki/Butch_Huskey" title="Butch Huskey">Butch Huskey</a> wore the number throughout the rest of his Mets career because of a <a href="/wiki/Grandfather_clause" title="Grandfather clause">grandfather clause</a> placed on the retired number by MLB.<sup id="cite_ref-Robinson_#_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robinson_#-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mo_Vaughn" title="Mo Vaughn">Mo Vaughn</a> also wore 42 during his stint with the Mets, because of the same clause.<sup id="cite_ref-Robinson_#_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robinson_#-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On the final opening day at Shea Stadium, April 8, 2008, the Mets unveiled a sign bearing the name <a href="/wiki/William_Shea" title="William Shea">"Shea"</a> next to the team\'s retired numbers honoring William Shea and his contributions to the franchise.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2014, a special memorial logo honoring broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Kiner" title="Ralph Kiner">Ralph Kiner</a>, depicting a microphone along with his name and the years 1922\xe2\x80\x932014, was displayed at on the left field wall adjacent to, but not as a part of, the Mets\' retired numbers, from 2014 to 2016. In the 2016 Mets yearbook, a sidebar in an article on Mike Piazza\'s upcoming number retirement implies that Kiner has been "retired" a la William A. Shea.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>  This was confirmed when the Mets\' retired numbers were moved to the roof facade during the 2016 season to accommodate Mike Piazza\'s #31; the Kiner logo was placed next to the Shea and Jackie Robinson numbers, no longer separated from the others.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Numbers_out_of_circulation_but_not_retired">Numbers out of circulation but not retired</span></h4>\n<ul><li><b>8</b>: Not issued since <a href="/wiki/Gary_Carter" title="Gary Carter">Gary Carter</a> was elected to the Hall of Fame in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-Mets_by_the_Numbers_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mets_by_the_Numbers-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> When the Mets honored Carter, they did not retire number 8, but instead gave him a replica of his Hall of Fame plaque depicting him as a Met instead of an Expo. <a href="/wiki/Desi_Relaford" title="Desi Relaford">Desi Relaford</a> was the last Mets player to wear No. 8; <a href="/wiki/Matt_Galante" title="Matt Galante">Matt Galante</a>, a coach, later wore the number. After Carter\'s death, the Mets honored him in a ceremony on opening day 2012, where they unveiled the "Kid 8" memorial logo (also worn on the uniform sleeve) on the outfield fence. However, the number 8 is still not officially retired.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>17</b>: Since <a href="/wiki/Keith_Hernandez" title="Keith Hernandez">Keith Hernandez</a>\'s retirement, his number 17 has been worn by <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Appier" title="Kevin Appier">Kevin Appier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dae-Sung_Koo" title="Dae-Sung Koo">Dae-Sung Koo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Lima" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Lima">Jos\xc3\xa9 Lima</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Newhan" title="David Newhan">David Newhan</a>, and lastly by <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Tat%C3%ADs" title="Fernando Tat\xc3\xads">Fernando Tat\xc3\xads</a>, who played for the Mets from 2008 to 2010. It has not been re-issued to any player or coach since 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>24</b>: Issued to two players since the retirement of <a href="/wiki/Willie_Mays" title="Willie Mays">Willie Mays</a>. Then-owner <a href="/wiki/Joan_Whitney_Payson" title="Joan Whitney Payson">Joan Whitney Payson</a> had promised Mays it would not be issued again. The first time was to first baseman-outfielder <a href="/wiki/Kelvin_Torve" title="Kelvin Torve">Kelvin Torve</a> in 1990, by mistake. The second was to <a href="/wiki/Rickey_Henderson" title="Rickey Henderson">Rickey Henderson</a> in 1999\xe2\x80\x932000 as a player and again in 2007 as a coach.<sup id="cite_ref-Mets_by_the_Numbers_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mets_by_the_Numbers-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subway_Series:_New_York_Yankees">Subway Series: New York Yankees</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mets%E2%80%93Yankees_rivalry" title="Mets\xe2\x80\x93Yankees rivalry">Mets\xe2\x80\x93Yankees rivalry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Subway_Series" title="Subway Series">Subway Series</a></div>\n<p>The Mets&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 New York Yankees rivalry is the latest incarnation of the <a href="/wiki/Subway_Series" title="Subway Series">Subway Series</a>, the competition between New York City\'s teams, the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> Mets. Until <a href="/wiki/Interleague_play" title="Interleague play">Interleague play</a> started, the two teams had only met in exhibition games. Since the inception of interleague play the two teams have met every regular season since 1997, and since 1999 they have met six times each season, playing two three-game series, one in each team\'s ballpark. From the 2013 season however the number of games was reduced to four, two at each ballpark with the Mets winning six of the last eight games in that span. They have made the postseason in the same year four times: 1999, 2000, 2006, and 2015, and faced off in the <a href="/wiki/2000_World_Series" title="2000 World Series">2000 World Series</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Atlanta_Braves">Atlanta Braves</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Braves%E2%80%93Mets_rivalry" title="Braves\xe2\x80\x93Mets rivalry">Braves\xe2\x80\x93Mets rivalry</a></div>\n<p>The Braves\xe2\x80\x93Mets <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_rivalries" title="Major League Baseball rivalries">rivalry</a> is a rivalry between two teams in the <a href="/wiki/National_League_East" title="National League East">National League East</a>, featuring the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Atlanta Braves</a> and the Mets.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although their first major confrontation occurred when the Mets swept the Braves in the <a href="/wiki/1969_National_League_Championship_Series" title="1969 National League Championship Series">1969 NLCS</a>, en route to their first <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> championship, the first playoff series won by an expansion team (also the first playoff appearance by an expansion team), the rivalry did not become especially heated until the 1990s, when division realignment put the Mets and the Braves in the same division.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>  The two teams faced each other again in the <a href="/wiki/1999_National_League_Championship_Series" title="1999 National League Championship Series">1999 NLCS</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/1999_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="1999 Atlanta Braves season">Braves</a> won the series four games to two. However, they would go on to lose to the <a href="/wiki/1999_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1999 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1999_World_Series" title="1999 World Series">1999 World Series</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philadelphia_Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mets%E2%80%93Phillies_rivalry" title="Mets\xe2\x80\x93Phillies rivalry">Mets\xe2\x80\x93Phillies rivalry</a></div>\n<p>The rivalry between the Mets and the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a> from 2006 to 2008 was said to be among the "hottest" rivalries in the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Aside from several brawls in the 1980s, the rivalry remained low-key before the 2006 season,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> as the teams had seldom been equally good at the same time. Since 2006, the teams have battled for playoff position. The Mets won the division in 2006 and contended in 2007 and 2008, while the Phillies won five consecutive division titles from 2007 to 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The Phillies\' 2007 Eastern Division Title was won on the last day of the season as the Mets lost a seven-game lead with 17 games remaining while losing 12 of 18 games that season to the Phillies, including being swept at home in the first 3 games of the remaining 17, dropping their lead from 7 games to 3.5.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Staff">Staff</span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="background-color:#002D72;color:#FFFFFF;-moz-box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #FF5910, inset -2px -2px 0 #FF5910; -webkit-box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #FF5910, inset -2px -2px 0 #FF5910; box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #FF5910, inset -2px -2px 0 #FF5910;;">New York Mets staff\n</th></tr>\n\n<tr>\n<td>Office of the Chairman\n<ul><li>Owner/CEO \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Fred_Wilpon" title="Fred Wilpon">Fred Wilpon</a></li>\n<li>President \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Saul_Katz" title="Saul Katz">Saul Katz</a></li>\n<li>Chief Operating Officer \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Wilpon" title="Jeff Wilpon">Jeff Wilpon</a></li></ul>\n<p>Front Office\n</p>\n<ul><li>General Manager \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Alderson" title="Sandy Alderson">Sandy Alderson</a></li>\n<li>Vice President, Assistant General Manager \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/John_Ricco" title="John Ricco">John Ricco</a></li>\n<li>Special Assistant to General Manager \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/J.P._Ricciardi" class="mw-redirect" title="J.P. Ricciardi">J.P. Major League Baseball team rosters">All MLB rosters</a></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="New_York_Mets_Foundation">New York Mets Foundation</span></h2>\n<p>A registered 501(c)(3) charity, the New York Mets Foundation is the philanthropic organization of the New York Mets. Founded in 1963, it funds and promotes charitable causes in the Mets community. One of these causes is <a href="/wiki/Tuesday%27s_Children" title="Tuesday&#39;s Children">Tuesday\'s Children</a>, is a non-profit family service organization that "has made a long term commitment to meet the needs of every family who lost a loved one in the terrorist attacks on September 11, 2001".<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The Mets host the annual Welcome Home Dinner, which raised over $550,000 for the Mets Foundation in 2012. All proceeds were distributed to Katz Institute for Women\'s Health and Katz Women\'s Hospitals of North Shore-LIJ Health System and The Leukemia &amp; Lymphoma Society.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Owners_and_executives">Owners and executives</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_New_York_Mets_owners_and_executives" title="List of New York Mets owners and executives">List of New York Mets owners and executives</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="New_York_Mets_broadcasters">New York Mets broadcasters</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_New_York_Mets_broadcasters" title="List of New York Mets broadcasters">List of New York Mets broadcasters</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span></h3>\n<p>Most Mets games are carried by <a href="/wiki/SportsNet_New_York" title="SportsNet New York">SportsNet New York</a> (SNY), a joint venture of the Mets and <a href="/wiki/NBC_Sports_Regional_Networks" title="NBC Sports Regional Networks">NBC Sports Regional Networks</a>. The team\'s terrestrial broadcast home is <a href="/wiki/WPIX" title="WPIX">WPIX</a>, where the team has broadcast games since 1999.\n</p><p>Longtime Mets radio announcer <a href="/wiki/Gary_Cohen" title="Gary Cohen">Gary Cohen</a> does the play-by-play, having moved to television with the launch of SNY in 2006. Former Mets <a href="/wiki/Keith_Hernandez" title="Keith Hernandez">Keith Hernandez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ron_Darling" title="Ron Darling">Ron Darling</a> are the color commentators.\n</p><p>In early January 2016, Keith Hernandez re-signed with SNY. Reports indicate that Hernandez received a raise and three-year contract.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span></h3>\n<p>As of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_Mets&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the Mets\' radio flagship is <a href="/wiki/WOR_(AM)" title="WOR (AM)">WOR</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The Mets were previously carried by <a href="/wiki/WFAN_(AM)" title="WFAN (AM)">WFAN</a>, which inherited the team\'s broadcast rights from <a href="/wiki/WEPN_(AM)#WHN" title="WEPN (AM)">WHN</a> when it took over its frequency in 1987, and <a href="/wiki/WFAN-FM" title="WFAN-FM">WFAN-FM</a>, which simulcasts the AM signal. Spanish language broadcasts are carried by <a href="/wiki/WEPN_(AM)" title="WEPN (AM)">WEPN</a>.\n</p><p>Since 2012, <a href="/wiki/Howie_Rose" title="Howie Rose">Howie Rose</a> and <a href="/wiki/Josh_Lewin" title="Josh Lewin">Josh Lewin</a> have been the radio broadcast team; they share play-by-play and analyst duties. Rose, who has spent much of his career covering the Mets, replaced <a href="/wiki/Bob_Murphy_(broadcaster)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bob Murphy (broadcaster)">Bob Murphy</a> as Gary Cohen\'s partner in 2004 following Murphy\'s retirement. Lewin joined the broadcast after the team parted ways with Wayne Hagin following the 2011 season. Pregame and postgame shows are hosted by <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Randazzo" class="mw-redirect" title="Wayne Randazzo">Wayne Randazzo</a>.\n</p><p>Lewin is also the radio voice for <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Bruins" title="UCLA Bruins">UCLA Bruins</a> football and basketball; Lewin\'s duties preclude him from calling games on weekends during the last month of the season, during which Randazzo steps in.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Minor_league_affiliations">Minor league affiliations</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article:
